<p><b>Clarence Clyde Seedorf</b> (<small>Dutch pronunciation:&#32;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">[ˈklɛrəns ˈseːdɔrf]</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nl-Clarence_Seedorf.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/29/Nl-Clarence_Seedorf.ogg" class="internal" title="Nl-Clarence Seedorf.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; born 1 April 1976) is a Dutch professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> coach and former player. He was most recently the manager of the <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">Cameroon national team</a>.
</p><p>Regarded by many as one of the best <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">midfielders</a> of his generation, in 2004, he was chosen by <a href="/wiki/Pel%C3%A9" title="Pelé">Pelé</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_100" title="FIFA 100">FIFA 100</a>. Seedorf is one of the most decorated Dutch players ever, and has won domestic and continental titles while playing for clubs in the Netherlands, Spain, Italy and Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> He is considered one of the most successful players in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> history, as he is the first, and currently the only, player to have won the Champions League with three clubs – once with <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a>, in <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_UEFA_Champions_League" title="1994–95 UEFA Champions League">1995</a>, once with <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." class="mw-redirect" title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a>, in <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_UEFA_Champions_League" title="1997–98 UEFA Champions League">1998</a> and twice with <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a>, in <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2002–03 UEFA Champions League">2003</a> and <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2006–07 UEFA Champions League">2007</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> At international level, he represented the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands</a> on 87 occasions, and took part at three <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Football_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA European Football Championship">UEFA European Football Championships</a> (<a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1996" title="UEFA Euro 1996">1996</a>, <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2000" title="UEFA Euro 2000">2000</a>, <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004" title="UEFA Euro 2004">2004</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998 FIFA World Cup</a>, reaching the semi-finals of the latter three tournaments.
</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>
</ul>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarence_Seedorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Paramaribo" title="Paramaribo">Paramaribo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Clarence_Seedorf_-_A.C._Milan_squad_2011/2012_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clarence_Seedorf_-_A.C._Milan_squad_2011/2012-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Seedorf was raised in <a href="/wiki/Almere" title="Almere">Almere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flevoland" title="Flevoland">Flevoland</a>, where he moved when he was two years old.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Growing up in a footballing family, with both his younger brothers Jürgen and <a href="/wiki/Chedric_Seedorf" title="Chedric Seedorf">Chedric Seedorf</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and his father former player and talent agent Johann Seedorf, Clarence began his career at the age of six in the youth ranks of his local amateur sides VV AS '80 and Real Almere,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> before being discovered and recruited to the ranks of nearby Dutch giants <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a> by Urgent Scoutingteam, the talent agency set up by <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff" title="Johan Cruyff">Johan Cruyff</a>, and which was responsible for recruiting the likes of <a href="/wiki/Frank_de_Boer" title="Frank de Boer">Frank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ronald_de_Boer" title="Ronald de Boer">Ronald de Boer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Davids" title="Edgar Davids">Edgar Davids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Witschge" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Witschge">Robert Witschge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Kluivert" title="Patrick Kluivert">Patrick Kluivert</a> to the club as well.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Following in their brother's footsteps, under the guidance of their father and talent agent, Seedorf's siblings, as well as cousin <a href="/wiki/Stefano_Seedorf" title="Stefano Seedorf">Stefano</a>, would later also join the ranks of Ajax. He is also a pundit on BBC.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarence_Seedorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ajax">Ajax</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarence_Seedorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ajax">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As a product of the famed <a href="/wiki/Ajax_Youth_Academy" title="Ajax Youth Academy">Ajax Youth Academy</a>, Seedorf started his career as a right midfielder for Ajax during the early 1990s. He made his professional debut on 29 November 1992 against <a href="/wiki/FC_Groningen" title="FC Groningen">Groningen</a> at the age of 16 years and 242 days, making him the youngest-ever debutant for Ajax, at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> He quickly established himself as the first choice on his position under manager <a href="/wiki/Louis_van_Gaal" title="Louis van Gaal">Louis van Gaal</a>, and in the <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_Eredivisie" title="1993–94 Eredivisie">1993–94 season</a>, his second with the club, he helped the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>-based side win the <a href="/wiki/Treble_(association_football)" title="Treble (association football)">treble</a>, securing the <a href="/wiki/Eredivisie" title="Eredivisie">Eredivisie</a> title, the <a href="/wiki/KNVB_Cup" title="KNVB Cup">KNVB Cup</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruijff_Shield" class="mw-redirect" title="Johan Cruijff Shield">Dutch Super Cup</a> in the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Among his teammates was none other than <a href="/wiki/Frank_Rijkaard" title="Frank Rijkaard">Frank Rijkaard</a>, the player he used to idolise in his younger days<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>.
</p><p>The following season saw Seedorf help his side secure consecutive Super Cup and Eredivisie titles, as well as help his side to their fourth <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">European Cup</a> trophy, winning the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_UEFA_Champions_League" title="1994–95 UEFA Champions League">1994–95 UEFA Champions League</a> after defeating <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1995_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="1995 UEFA Champions League Final">final</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> He played a key role in the final before being replaced in the 53rd minute by striker <a href="/wiki/Nwankwo_Kanu" title="Nwankwo Kanu">Nwankwo Kanu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Kluivert" title="Patrick Kluivert">Patrick Kluivert</a> scored a late goal to lift Ajax to a 1–0 victory over the Italian giants,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> who Seedorf would later go on to represent for a decade.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> While at Ajax, he was part of a trio known as "<a href="/wiki/De_kabel" title="De kabel">De kabel</a>", composed of Edgar Davids, Patrick Kluivert and himself. Later, <a href="/wiki/Winston_Bogarde" title="Winston Bogarde">Winston Bogarde</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Reiziger" title="Michael Reiziger">Michael Reiziger</a> would be added to the group to make it a quintet; what had started as a friendship was then taken over during the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1996" title="UEFA Euro 1996">UEFA Euro 1996</a> to describe the group.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sampdoria">Sampdoria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarence_Seedorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Sampdoria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Opting not to extend his contract with Ajax following their European success and the <a href="/wiki/Bosman_ruling" title="Bosman ruling">Bosman ruling</a>, Seedorf signed a one-year contract with Italian <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> side <a href="/wiki/U.C._Sampdoria" title="U.C. Sampdoria">Sampdoria</a> instead.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> While not able to obtain any silverware in his first season at his new club, Seedorf appeared in 32 matches, scoring three goals helping his side to an eighth-place finish in the league table, all the while maintaining the form he had demonstrated at Ajax in the past. Seedorf was then able to secure a transfer to <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." class="mw-redirect" title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a>, moving to the Spanish <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> by the end of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Real_Madrid">Real Madrid</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarence_Seedorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Real Madrid">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Seedorf moved to Real Madrid in 1996,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> where he was virtually ever present for <i>Los Blancos</i> in his first three seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In his <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_Real_Madrid_C.F._season" class="mw-redirect" title="1996–97 Real Madrid C.F. season">first season</a>, he helped the team regain the La Liga title, while in his second season, <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_Real_Madrid_C.F._season" class="mw-redirect" title="1997–98 Real Madrid C.F. season">1997–98</a>, he played a major role in the team's <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_UEFA_Champions_League" title="1997–98 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> success, as Madrid secured a 1–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1998_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="1998 UEFA Champions League Final">final</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> earning his second Champions League title of his career.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clarence_Seedorf_and_Mesut_%C3%96zil.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Clarence_Seedorf_and_Mesut_%C3%96zil.jpg/200px-Clarence_Seedorf_and_Mesut_%C3%96zil.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Clarence_Seedorf_and_Mesut_%C3%96zil.jpg/300px-Clarence_Seedorf_and_Mesut_%C3%96zil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Clarence_Seedorf_and_Mesut_%C3%96zil.jpg/400px-Clarence_Seedorf_and_Mesut_%C3%96zil.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="803" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clarence_Seedorf_and_Mesut_%C3%96zil.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Seedorf playing against former club Real Madrid. On the left is <a href="/wiki/Mesut_%C3%96zil" title="Mesut Özil">Mesut Özil</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>While playing for Real Madrid, Seedorf scored a notable long-range goal against <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a> in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
At the end of the <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_Real_Madrid_C.F._season" class="mw-redirect" title="1998–99 Real Madrid C.F. season">1998–99 season</a>, Madrid and Juventus wanted to swap Seedorf for <a href="/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane" title="Zinedine Zidane">Zinedine Zidane</a>, but the deal did not go through and the French playmaker waited two more years before joining Real Madrid.
</p><p>Starting from the summer of 1999, Seedorf's role at Real Madrid became less prominent during the tenue of Dutch manager <a href="/wiki/Guus_Hiddink" title="Guus Hiddink">Guus Hiddink</a> at the club. He was eventually transferred back to Italy during the <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Real_Madrid_C.F._season" class="mw-redirect" title="1999–2000 Real Madrid C.F. season">1999–2000 season</a>, this time to <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a>, for a fee about 44 billion <a href="/wiki/Italian_lira" title="Italian lira">Italian lira</a> (approximately €23 million).<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inter_Milan">Inter Milan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarence_Seedorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Inter Milan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 24 December 1999, Seedorf moved to Inter in a $24.35 million deal after cementing his place in the Real Madrid midfield for over three years.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Despite helping the team to the <a href="/wiki/Coppa_Italia" title="Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> final later that season – a 2–1 aggregate loss to <a href="/wiki/S.S._Lazio" title="S.S. Lazio">Lazio</a> where Seedorf scored Inter's only goal<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> – Seedorf could not help bring any major silverware to the club. Nonetheless, he is remembered by many Inter fans for his two goals against Juventus in a 2–2 draw on 9 March 2002, both of which were superb long-range efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="AC_Milan">AC Milan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarence_Seedorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: AC Milan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clarence_Seedorf_Emirates_Cup_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Clarence_Seedorf_Emirates_Cup_2010.jpg/170px-Clarence_Seedorf_Emirates_Cup_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Clarence_Seedorf_Emirates_Cup_2010.jpg/255px-Clarence_Seedorf_Emirates_Cup_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Clarence_Seedorf_Emirates_Cup_2010.jpg/340px-Clarence_Seedorf_Emirates_Cup_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="5184" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clarence_Seedorf_Emirates_Cup_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Seedorf with Milan in a friendly against <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>After two years with Inter, Seedorf moved to their city rivals <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">AC Milan</a> in 2002, in an exchange with <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Coco" title="Francesco Coco">Francesco Coco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Seedorf won the <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_Coppa_Italia" title="2002–03 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> with Milan in 2003, the first time they had won the competition in 26 years. In the same season, Seedorf gained his third Champions League medal, becoming the first player to win the Champions League with three clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The all-Italian <a href="/wiki/2003_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2003 UEFA Champions League Final">final</a> saw Milan beat Juventus on penalties after a 0–0 draw, despite Seedorf failing to convert his own penalty. The following season, <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_A.C._Milan_season" title="2003–04 A.C. Milan season">2003–04</a>, Seedorf played a role in the Milan side that won the <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Serie_A" title="2003–04 Serie A">Serie A</a> title. It was Seedorf's fourth national league title of his career, following his two Dutch title wins with Ajax and his one Spanish win with Real Madrid.
</p><p>Seedorf played a major role as Milan reached the Champions League final again in <a href="/wiki/2005_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2005 UEFA Champions League Final">2005</a>, scoring the only goal of the game in their opening group match against <a href="/wiki/FC_Shakhtar_Donetsk" title="FC Shakhtar Donetsk">Shakhtar Donetsk</a> on 14 September 2004 and appearing in all 13 competition matches.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> He started the match, played in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, against <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> in which Milan contrived to lose a 3–0 lead, eventually losing on penalties after a 3–3 draw; Seedorf did not take a spot-kick.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Milan also finished runners-up in the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Serie_A" title="2004–05 Serie A">Serie A</a>, seven points behind champions Juventus, although Juventus were stripped of the title and Milan docked points for match-fixing.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Calciopoli" class="mw-redirect" title="Calciopoli">match-fixing scandal tarnished Serie A</a> and Milan were weakened by the scandal but were allowed to continue in Europe the following season, which led to their top players remaining with the club. Seedorf's role as foil to midfielder <a href="/wiki/Kak%C3%A1" title="Kaká">Kaká</a> became increasingly impressive as the pair combined in style to score and supply the goals which drove Milan past <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> to another <a href="/wiki/2007_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2007 UEFA Champions League Final">Champions League final</a>, again against Liverpool. This time, however, they defeated them 2–1 in <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>, with Seedorf collecting his fourth Champions League medal. In that same year, Seedorf was a part of a Milan squad which won the <a href="/wiki/2007_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2007 FIFA Club World Cup">FIFA Club World Cup</a>, becoming the first European player to win the trophy with three clubs (Ajax in 1995 and Real Madrid in 1998). He ended up winning the Silver Ball for the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seedorf_with_Addo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Seedorf_with_Addo.jpg/170px-Seedorf_with_Addo.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Seedorf_with_Addo.jpg/255px-Seedorf_with_Addo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Seedorf_with_Addo.jpg/340px-Seedorf_with_Addo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="390" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seedorf_with_Addo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clarence Seedorf in action for <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a> against <a href="/wiki/Eric_Addo" title="Eric Addo">Eric Addo</a> of <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV</a> in a friendly game on 3 August 2007 at the <a href="/wiki/Lokomotiv_Stadium_(Moscow)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lokomotiv Stadium (Moscow)">Lokomotiv Stadium</a>, Moscow.</div></div></div>
<p>At the end of the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2006–07 UEFA Champions League">2006–07 season</a>, Seedorf was voted best midfielder of the Champions League. He played his 100th game in the Champions League on 4 December against <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a>.
</p><p>With Milan, Seedorf formed a formidable midfield partnership with <a href="/wiki/Gennaro_Gattuso" title="Gennaro Gattuso">Gennaro Gattuso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Pirlo" title="Andrea Pirlo">Andrea Pirlo</a>, which began since the <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_A.C._Milan_season" title="2002–03 A.C. Milan season">2002–03 season</a>. This midfield trio was still used in the starting line-up until the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_A.C._Milan_season" title="2011–12 A.C. Milan season">2011–12 season</a> (Pirlo left the <i>Rossoneri</i> in the summer of 2011), although their form had been declining. Under the guidance of coach <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Ancelotti" title="Carlo Ancelotti">Carlo Ancelotti</a>, their role was to support an attacking midfielder, whether it be <a href="/wiki/Rivaldo" title="Rivaldo">Rivaldo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rui_Costa" title="Rui Costa">Rui Costa</a>, Kaká or <a href="/wiki/Ronaldinho" title="Ronaldinho">Ronaldinho</a>.
</p><p>Seedorf became the foreigner with the most appearances for Milan following a game against his former club, Sampdoria, which he scored in. At 395 appearances, he passed <a href="/wiki/Nils_Liedholm" title="Nils Liedholm">Nils Liedholm</a> for this historic milestone. During the Sampdoria game, he also became the ninth-highest scoring foreigner for Milan, with 58 goals.
On 29 March 2010, Seedorf was the target of racist chants from Lazio fans in a 1–1 draw, which led to the Rome-based club being given a €15,000 fine by the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Football_Federation" title="Italian Football Federation">Italian Football Federation</a> (FIGC). This led the Italy's players' union want racism stamped out in Serie A.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Seedorf won his second <i><a href="/wiki/Scudetto" title="Scudetto">Scudetto</a></i> with Milan in the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Serie_A" title="2010–11 Serie A">2010–11 Serie A</a> season, where he once again played a vital role. He scored four goals and made 36 appearances in the 2010–11 season.
Seedorf added yet another medal to his trophy cabinet in the first official game of the 2011–12 season, where he played the full 90 minutes in a 2–1 comeback win over rivals Inter Milan in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Supercoppa_Italiana" title="2011 Supercoppa Italiana">Supercoppa Italiana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> He scored the winning goal of Milan's first win of the 2011–12 Serie A campaign, a 1–0 defeat of <a href="/wiki/A.C._Cesena" title="A.C. Cesena">Cesena</a> on 24 September.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Seedorf was ranked seventh of the 20 best players of the Champions League, a list which was compiled in 2012 to commemorate the 20th anniversary of the competition. The ranking was done by <i>Champions</i>, the official magazine of UEFA.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> On 14 May, he said that he was playing his last match with Milan against Novara that day. He also confirmed that he would continue to play football for another club. On 21 June, Seedorf held a press conference announcing his departure from Milan, stating, "I am leaving after 10 wonderful years... I leave a family" after playing for the <i>Rossoneri</i> for a decade and winning two Champions League, two <i>Scudettos</i> and a Coppa Italia.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Club CEO <a href="/wiki/Adriano_Galliani" title="Adriano Galliani">Adriano Galliani</a> spoke of Seedorf following the player's departure in the highest regard, stating, "When Milan played well, which happened often, each and every time it occurred Seedorf played an amazing match. He is a world class player."<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Botafogo">Botafogo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarence_Seedorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Botafogo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seedorf_(10663636224).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Seedorf_%2810663636224%29.jpg/220px-Seedorf_%2810663636224%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Seedorf_%2810663636224%29.jpg/330px-Seedorf_%2810663636224%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Seedorf_%2810663636224%29.jpg/440px-Seedorf_%2810663636224%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3257" data-file-height="2171" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seedorf_(10663636224).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Seedorf playing for Botafogo in 2013</div></div></div>
<p>On 30 June 2012, Seedorf signed a two-year contract with Brazilian club <a href="/wiki/Botafogo_de_Futebol_e_Regatas" title="Botafogo de Futebol e Regatas">Botafogo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The veteran midfielder made his debut with the club on 22 July against <a href="/wiki/Gremio_Foot-Ball_Porto_Alegrense" class="mw-redirect" title="Gremio Foot-Ball Porto Alegrense">Grêmio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> On 5 August, Seedorf scored his first goal for Botafogo, curling in a <a href="/wiki/Direct_free_kick" title="Direct free kick">free kick</a> against <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Clube_Goianiense" title="Atlético Clube Goianiense">Atlético Goianiense</a>. On 5 September, Seedorf scored two goals and made an assist against <a href="/wiki/Cruzeiro_Esporte_Clube" title="Cruzeiro Esporte Clube">Cruzeiro</a>, helping Botafogo to a 3–1 victory.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> On 3 February 2013, for the first time on his career, Seedorf scored a hat-trick against <a href="/wiki/Maca%C3%A9_Esporte_Futebol_Clube" title="Macaé Esporte Futebol Clube">Macaé</a>, his first game as a starter that year. Before that game, Seedorf played the second half against <a href="/wiki/Fluminense_Football_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Fluminense Football Club">Fluminense</a> and made a good assist to <a href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar_(footballer)" title="Bolívar (footballer)">Bolívar</a>, who scored the match's equalizer.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>On 10 March 2013, Seedorf won his first title with Botafogo: the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%A7a_Guanabara" title="Taça Guanabara">Taça Guanabara</a>, the first round of 2013 <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Carioca" title="Campeonato Carioca">Campeonato Carioca</a>. On 5 May, he won the second round of 2013 Campeonato Carioca – 2013 Taça Rio – against Fluminense. That is also the day of his first official title for Botafogo, the 2013 Campeonato Carioca, as the team won both rounds and no final match was needed. On 6 June, Seedorf scored his 100th goal in domestic league play: 11 with Ajax, 3 with Sampdoria, 15 with Real Madrid, 8 with Inter, 47 with Milan and 16 with Botafogo. On 14 January 2014, Seedorf announced his retirement from professional football. He announced that he is ending his playing career to take up the manager position at Milan following the sacking of <a href="/wiki/Massimiliano_Allegri" title="Massimiliano Allegri">Massimiliano Allegri</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarence_Seedorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Due to Surinamese rules against <a href="/wiki/Multiple_citizenship" title="Multiple citizenship">dual citizenship</a>, players who take <a href="/wiki/Dutch_nationality_law" title="Dutch nationality law">Dutch citizenship</a> are no longer eligible to represent the Netherlands' <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">former colony</a>. He received his first callup on 14 December 1994 at the age of 18 against <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_national_football_team" title="Luxembourg national football team">Luxembourg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Seedorf scored on his debut, helping his team to a 5–0 victory in a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1996_qualifying_Group_5" title="UEFA Euro 1996 qualifying Group 5">UEFA Euro 1996 qualifying</a> match.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Seedorf was in the Dutch squad for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Football_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA European Football Championship">UEFA European Championships</a> in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1996" title="UEFA Euro 1996">1996</a>, where his penalty miss proved decisive in the quarter-final shootout defeat to <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> He also appeared for the Netherlands at <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2000" title="UEFA Euro 2000">Euro 2000</a> and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004" title="UEFA Euro 2004">2004</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998 FIFA World Cup</a>, reaching the semi-finals in all three of these tournaments.
</p><p>On 12 November 2006, Seedorf was recalled for the first time since June 2004 as a replacement for the injured <a href="/wiki/Wesley_Sneijder" title="Wesley Sneijder">Wesley Sneijder</a>. He started and played the full 90&#160;minutes in a 1–1 friendly draw against <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a>. Seedorf won the last of his 87 caps for the Netherlands in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In the Euro 2008 qualifiers against <a href="/wiki/Romania_national_football_team" title="Romania national football team">Romania</a> (0–0 at home) and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia_national_football_team" title="Slovenia national football team">Slovenia</a> (1–0 away win), Seedorf played four and six&#160;minutes respectively. There were doubts on his position within the national team, as <a href="/wiki/Marco_van_Basten" title="Marco van Basten">Marco van Basten</a> favoured younger players such as <a href="/wiki/Rafael_van_der_Vaart" title="Rafael van der Vaart">Rafael van der Vaart</a>, Wesley Sneijder and <a href="/wiki/Robin_van_Persie" title="Robin van Persie">Robin van Persie</a>. On 13 May 2008, Seedorf announced that he would not take part in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008" title="UEFA Euro 2008">UEFA Euro 2008</a> due to his ongoing personal conflict with Van Basten.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarence_Seedorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jersey_of_Clarence_Seedorf.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Jersey_of_Clarence_Seedorf.jpg/170px-Jersey_of_Clarence_Seedorf.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Jersey_of_Clarence_Seedorf.jpg/255px-Jersey_of_Clarence_Seedorf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Jersey_of_Clarence_Seedorf.jpg/340px-Jersey_of_Clarence_Seedorf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2322" data-file-height="4128" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jersey_of_Clarence_Seedorf.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Seedorf's number 10 Milan jersey in the <a href="/wiki/San_Siro" title="San Siro">San Siro</a> museum</div></div></div>
<p>Seedorf was a well-rounded, hardworking and versatile player, who was gifted with strength, pace, stamina and notable physical attributes, which allowed him to play anywhere in <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">midfield</a> and contribute both offensively and defensively, due to his significant tactical intelligence; although he primarily served as a <a href="/wiki/Playmaker" title="Playmaker">playmaker</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Central_midfielder" class="mw-redirect" title="Central midfielder">centre</a>, throughout his career he was also deployed as an <a href="/wiki/Attacking_midfielder" class="mw-redirect" title="Attacking midfielder">attacking midfielder</a>, on the <a href="/wiki/Winger_(association_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Winger (association football)">wing</a>, or in a <a href="/wiki/Holding_midfielder" class="mw-redirect" title="Holding midfielder">holding</a> or <a href="/wiki/Box-to-box_midfielder" class="mw-redirect" title="Box-to-box midfielder">box-to-box</a> role.<sup id="cite_ref-Unlike_Simeone&#39;s_Atletico,_Seedorf&#39;s_AC_Milan_still_searching_for_identity_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unlike_Simeone&#39;s_Atletico,_Seedorf&#39;s_AC_Milan_still_searching_for_identity-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Seedorf_reaches_Milan_landmark_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seedorf_reaches_Milan_landmark-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-acmilan.com_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acmilan.com-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A world class midfielder, in addition to his fitness and athletic characteristics, as well as his ability to break down opposing plays and win back possession,<sup id="cite_ref-Unlike_Simeone&#39;s_Atletico,_Seedorf&#39;s_AC_Milan_still_searching_for_identity_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unlike_Simeone&#39;s_Atletico,_Seedorf&#39;s_AC_Milan_still_searching_for_identity-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Seedorf_reaches_Milan_landmark_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seedorf_reaches_Milan_landmark-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> he was an elegant, creative player and an excellent <a href="/wiki/Dribbling#Association_football" title="Dribbling">dribbler</a>, possessing outstanding technique, ball skills and vision, which enabled him to retain possession when under pressure and subsequently lay the ball off to an on-rushing teammate;<sup id="cite_ref-AC_Milan_Pen_Pics_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AC_Milan_Pen_Pics-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> he was also an accurate passer and <a href="/wiki/Cross_(football)" title="Cross (football)">crosser</a> of the ball.<sup id="cite_ref-Unlike_Simeone&#39;s_Atletico,_Seedorf&#39;s_AC_Milan_still_searching_for_identity_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unlike_Simeone&#39;s_Atletico,_Seedorf&#39;s_AC_Milan_still_searching_for_identity-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-acmilan.com_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acmilan.com-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Seedorf was also capable of scoring goals due to his powerful, accurate striking ability from distance with either foot;<sup id="cite_ref-Unlike_Simeone&#39;s_Atletico,_Seedorf&#39;s_AC_Milan_still_searching_for_identity_47-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unlike_Simeone&#39;s_Atletico,_Seedorf&#39;s_AC_Milan_still_searching_for_identity-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Seedorf_reaches_Milan_landmark_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seedorf_reaches_Milan_landmark-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> furthermore, he was an effective free kick taker.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Despite his physical, energetic, and tenacious style of play, Seedorf was regarded as a correct player, and was sent off only two times in his entire career. In addition to his success and footballing skills, Seedorf has also been praised for his longevity as a footballer.<sup id="cite_ref-Unlike_Simeone&#39;s_Atletico,_Seedorf&#39;s_AC_Milan_still_searching_for_identity_47-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unlike_Simeone&#39;s_Atletico,_Seedorf&#39;s_AC_Milan_still_searching_for_identity-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Managerial_career">Managerial career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarence_Seedorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Managerial career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Seedorf was appointed the new head coach of Milan on 16 January 2014, terminating his contract with Botafogo early in order to take on the managerial role, with Milan languishing in 11th in the Serie A table. On 19 January, he won his first managerial match, played against <a href="/wiki/Hellas_Verona_F.C." title="Hellas Verona F.C.">Hellas Verona</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Mario_Balotelli" title="Mario Balotelli">Mario Balotelli</a> scoring the lone goal of the game.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite overseeing the club's first five-match winning run since 2011, and first Serie A victory in the <a href="/wiki/Derby_della_Madonnina" title="Derby della Madonnina">Milan derby</a> against Inter since 2011, Seedorf was dismissed by Milan on 9 June 2014 after just four months on the job, with <a href="/wiki/Filippo_Inzaghi" title="Filippo Inzaghi">Filippo Inzaghi</a> being named as his successor.<sup id="cite_ref-AC_Milan_sacks_manager_Clarence_Seedorf_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AC_Milan_sacks_manager_Clarence_Seedorf-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> During the Dutchman's time at the helm of the club, Milan gained a total of 35 out of a possible 57 points - the fourth-most out of all Serie A sides (one less than Napoli's corresponding total and six less than Roma's).
</p><p>Seedorf was appointed manager of <a href="/wiki/China_League_One" title="China League One">China League One</a> team <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_F.C." title="Shenzhen F.C.">Shenzhen F.C.</a> in July 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>  but was replaced five months later by <a href="/wiki/Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson" title="Sven-Göran Eriksson">Sven-Göran Eriksson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> A year later Seedorf joined Brazilian club <a href="/wiki/Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Paranaense" class="mw-redirect" title="Clube Atlético Paranaense">Atlético Paranaense</a> as both a coach and a sporting director<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Within a month the deal was cancelled after both parties failed to reach an agreement.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In February 2018, Seedorf was appointed as manager of Spanish club <a href="/wiki/Deportivo_de_La_Coru%C3%B1a" title="Deportivo de La Coruña">Deportivo de La Coruña</a> for the remainder of the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_in_Spanish_football" title="2017–18 in Spanish football">2017–18</a> season.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Seedorf led the team to just two wins in sixteen matches, Deportivo were relegated from <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_La_Liga" title="2017–18 La Liga">La Liga</a>, and at the end of the season he left the club.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After a deal with Sven-Göran Eriksson could not be agreed, the <a href="/wiki/Cameroonian_Football_Federation" title="Cameroonian Football Federation">Fédération Camerounaise de Football</a> appointed Seedorf as the manager of the <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">Cameroon national team</a> in August 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> He was joined by former teammate <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Kluivert" title="Patrick Kluivert">Patrick Kluivert</a> as his assistant manager.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> However, after a disappointing <a href="/wiki/2019_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2019 Africa Cup of Nations">2019 Africa Cup of Nations</a>, where Cameroon was eliminated by <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_national_football_team" title="Nigeria national football team">Nigeria</a> in the round of sixteen after an unimpressive group stage, he was sacked in July 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life_and_other_work">Personal life and other work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clarence_Seedorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Personal life and other work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Princess_M%C3%A1xima,_Prince_Willem-Alexander_%26_Clarence_Seedorf.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Princess_M%C3%A1xima%2C_Prince_Willem-Alexander_%26_Clarence_Seedorf.jpg/220px-Princess_M%C3%A1xima%2C_Prince_Willem-Alexander_%26_Clarence_Seedorf.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Princess_M%C3%A1xima%2C_Prince_Willem-Alexander_%26_Clarence_Seedorf.jpg/330px-Princess_M%C3%A1xima%2C_Prince_Willem-Alexander_%26_Clarence_Seedorf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Princess_M%C3%A1xima%2C_Prince_Willem-Alexander_%26_Clarence_Seedorf.jpg/440px-Princess_M%C3%A1xima%2C_Prince_Willem-Alexander_%26_Clarence_Seedorf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="737" data-file-height="455" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Princess_M%C3%A1xima,_Prince_Willem-Alexander_%26_Clarence_Seedorf.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Seedorf with <a href="/wiki/Queen_M%C3%A1xima" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Máxima">Queen Máxima</a> and <a href="/wiki/King_Willem-Alexander_of_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="King Willem-Alexander of the Netherlands">King Willem-Alexander of the Netherlands</a>.</div></div></div> 
<p>Seedorf speaks six languages fluently:<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Dutch, English,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Italian, Portuguese, Spanish and <a href="/wiki/Sranan_Tongo" title="Sranan Tongo">Sranan Tongo</a>. He was often seen as a spiritual, intelligent and articulate figure in football,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> and in a 2011 interview, Seedorf stated that he was studying to obtain a master's degree in Business at the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Bocconi_University" title="Bocconi University">Bocconi University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> because of this, he earned the nickname "<i>il professore</i>" ("the professor") during his time playing at Milan.<sup id="cite_ref-Seedorf_reaches_Milan_landmark_48-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seedorf_reaches_Milan_landmark-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Seedorf is married to a Brazilian woman, Luviana Seedorf, with whom he owns a restaurant called <i>Finger's</i> in Milan. They have four children.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Seedorf has dabbled in media-related work during recent years. In 2009, he worked with <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> to run a column entitled "Seedorf responds", where once a month he would answer peoples' questions regarding football.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> He joined the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>'s team covering the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a> in South Africa, working as a <a href="/wiki/Pundit_(expert)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pundit (expert)">television pundit</a><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> He also presented a number of features for the BBC coverage, including one about <a href="/wiki/Robben_Island" title="Robben Island">Robben Island</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> He joined the BBC for their <i><a href="/wiki/Match_of_the_Day" title="Match of the Day">Match of the Day</a></i> Live coverage of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a>. He has also made appearances on <i><a href="/wiki/Match_of_the_Day_2" title="Match of the Day 2">Match of the Day 2</a></i> during the English football league season.
</p><p>Because of his strong connection with the country Suriname, where he was born, he is involved in many social development projects there. He built his own "<a href="/wiki/Clarence_Seedorf_Stadion" title="Clarence Seedorf Stadion">Clarence Seedorf Stadium</a>" in the <a href="/wiki/Para_District" title="Para District">district of Para</a> in Suriname. In this stadium, the Para Juniors League of Suriname is being held and the teams of the Suri Profs &amp; <a href="/wiki/S.V._The_Brothers" title="S.V. The Brothers">SV The Brothers</a> play there regularly. With his Champions for Children Foundation, he supports projects for good causes in Suriname.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> For this, Suriname has honoured him to Commandor of the High-Order of the Yellow Star, and recently in 2011, he was invested as a Knight of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Orange-Nassau" title="Order of Orange-Nassau">Order of Orange-Nassau</a> (OON).
</p><p>On 5 June 2009, Seedorf announced at a press conference after a meeting with <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a> that he had become the Nelson Mandela Foundation's latest Legacy Champion. He joins Patrice Motsepe, <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Sexwale" title="Tokyo Sexwale">Tokyo Sexwale</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Rockefeller" title="David Rockefeller">David Rockefeller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peggy_Dulany" title="Peggy Dulany">Peggy Dulany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, who are also members of a select group of <a href="/wiki/Philanthropy" title="Philanthropy">philanthropists</a> who are helping to ensure that Mr. Mandela's legacy lives on.
</p><p>In 2012 and 2014, Seedorf took part in <i><a href="/wiki/Soccer_Aid" title="Soccer Aid">Soccer Aid</a></i>, a charity match at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a> with former professional players and celebrities. He played for "The Rest of the World" team against England. In 2014, he scored a hat-trick, where The Rest of the World won 4–2; they raised over £4 million in total.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Clarence's nephew, <a href="/wiki/Collin_Seedorf" title="Collin Seedorf">Collin Seedorf</a>, is also a professional footballer, and currently plays for Dutch club, <a href="/wiki/FC_Eindhoven" title="FC Eindhoven">FC Eindhoven</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
